<div id="review_1712201953" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1712201953" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1712201953?book_show_action=true">Jul 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781473619791" href="/book/show/24956528-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kaylin by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=favorite-female-characters">favorite-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=recommended-to-me">recommended-to-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=disability-and-chronic-illness">disability-and-chronic-illness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1712201953" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15653111694603971973"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote> “All you can do, Rosemary – all any of us can do – is work to be something positive instead. That is a choice that every sapient must make every day of their life. The universe is what we make of it. It’s up to you to decide what part you will play.”</blockquote>
</i> <br/><br/>Before picking this up, I knew nothing about it—except <b>slow-burn, found-family in space.</b> And honestly that’s half my reading tastes in one sentence. <br/><br/>But what I didn’t know (and what elevated this book to ‘awesome’ status for me) is its</span>
  <span id="freeText15653111694603971973" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote> “All you can do, Rosemary – all any of us can do – is work to be something positive instead. That is a choice that every sapient must make every day of their life. The universe is what we make of it. It’s up to you to decide what part you will play.”</blockquote>
</i> <br /><br />Before picking this up, I knew nothing about it—except <b>slow-burn, found-family in space.</b> And honestly that’s half my reading tastes in one sentence. <br /><br />But what I didn’t know (and what elevated this book to ‘awesome’ status for me) is its <b>quietly and intimately optimistic take on humanity.</b>There are hundreds and hundreds of books that take a look at the depravity and violence of humanity. That analysis is valid... but it feels like one-half of the equation? Humanity is capable of great evil, but they are also capable of great <i>good.</i> Chambers doesn’t slam us over the head with it, or create an idealistic future, she simply shows us the everyday for these characters. <b>She gently shows us their motivations and capacity for ‘evil’ and then lets us revel in them choosing the opposite.</b> <br /><br />Another thing I loved was the small-scale of these decisions. This is definitely not a high-stakes space adventure, but instead we see the characters navigate new friendships and new lands. (There's also just a ton of <b>effortless diversity</b> here that leads to so many different viewpoints) There’s discussion of trauma and disability and loves lost. Something about these discussions seemed so <i>genuine,</i> and <b>I think these repeated-everyday decisions to love each other</b> say more about humanity’s capacity for goodness than any single rescue or good deed so far removed from real life. <br /><br />(Also I loved <b>every single character.</b> Kizzy and I are getting married next June, please RSVP)<br /><br /><b>It’s also just so much fun?</b> The whole premise of building worm-holes is inventive and exciting, but also leads to a huge, vast universe filled with so many species and worlds. Each new land the crew explored was complex, interesting, and oh-so creative. <b>This varied look at alien technology/language/species really is akin to old-school Star Trek</b> and something I’ve always loved in sci-fi. <br /><br />I do have to admit <b>there is almost zero plot.</b> This isn’t usually a problem for me, but the first half seemed to be going somewhere in particular… and we never really got there? Also, from her introduction it’s obvious Rosemary is hiding some secret about her past… but when it was finally revealed it felt <i>really</i> anticlimactic? It lead to some great discussions… it just didn’t feel worth all that build up??<br /><br /><b>Overall</b> <br /><br />This is zany, but also makes your heart ache in the good way. You can’t help but love the characters, even if they are following a plot that doesn’t really go anywhere.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15653111694603971973" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2030131175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2030131175" />
    <a title="Althea Ann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann"><img alt="Althea Ann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411566466p2/3846743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2030131175?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Althea Ann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Althea Ann" href="/user/show/3846743-althea-ann">Althea Ann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2030131175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10992678596508445048">The sequel to this was a Hugo nominee, so I figured I'd start with the first one, and requested it from the library. Well, maybe the sequel was a lot better, but unless I am assured of such a circumstance by a large and passionate crowd; I'm unlikely to bother to find out. <br/><br/>"The Long Way..." is a concept piece. It's a reaction to traditional space opera. In a "normal" sci-fi adventure, the scrappy crew of the "Wayfarer" would end up getting pulled into some kind of conflict bigger than themselves</span>
  <span id="freeText10992678596508445048" style="display:none">The sequel to this was a Hugo nominee, so I figured I'd start with the first one, and requested it from the library. Well, maybe the sequel was a lot better, but unless I am assured of such a circumstance by a large and passionate crowd; I'm unlikely to bother to find out. <br /><br />"The Long Way..." is a concept piece. It's a reaction to traditional space opera. In a "normal" sci-fi adventure, the scrappy crew of the "Wayfarer" would end up getting pulled into some kind of conflict bigger than themselves; something with universe-spanning ramifications; and would team up to defeat the enemy against overwhelming odds; regardless of the traitor in their midst... (Think Millennium Falcon, Han Solo, Lando Calrissian.) <br /><br />Becky Chambers has decided to make a point of telling a different story. One where no universe-shattering events happen; one where colleagues might be annoying but not actually evil; one where secrets turn out to be pretty mundane and have no meaningful effect when revealed. One where people spend most of their time worrying about things that aren't really important and doing boring crap.<br /><br />Now, I often very much enjoy stories that get "down to earth" and talk about what it's like to actually LIVE as an ordinary person in an imagined society: character-driven stories. I see other reviews of this book raving about the characterization here. I wasn't feeling it. I found the characters to be flat and stereotypical. The protagonist, Rosemary, didn't intrigue me at all. The captain is a generic "nice boss guy." Jenks is your stereotypical nerd guy. Lovey exists to show that AIs are people too. Some aliens and disabilities just to show that aliens and the disabled are people too. And let me not forget Kizzy the WACKY engineer gal who is (supposed to be) just SOOO ENDEARING! (God, I wished she was real so that I could literally strangle her.) And of course Corbin the biologist who's the cranky loner who no one really likes 'cause he likes his privacy and isn't wholly on board with the social lovefest that's life aboard the Wayfarer. (I could relate, considering - but you're not supposed to, dear readers! APPLAUD when he gets dragged into the fold and drinks the kool-aid, dammit!)<br /><br />There is a scene with pirates in this book. Even the pirates are reasonable and fairly "nice." Nothing much happens. There technically IS a plot device, but it's utterly forgettable. I mean, I genuinely don't remember what it was already. <br /><br />If you work in an office, or live in a shared apartment with several roommates: imagine if someone wrote daily letters to their parents about your office politics or quotidian household drama; making sure to not include anything too upsetting or serious. That's what reading this book is like. Chatty... and dull.<br /><br />I initially gave it two stars, but upon consideration, after the fact, I'm downgrading it to one, because not only did I not enjoy the book; I object to it on principle. I want my gritty betrayals and world-smashing explosions, dammit!<br /><br />Addendum: I see others comparing this book to both Ursula LeGuin (?!?!?) and Star Trek. For the record, I am an enthusiastic fan of both LeGuin and ST, and disagree strongly with both comparisons.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10992678596508445048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2320726998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2320726998" />
    <a title="Matthew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew"><img alt="Matthew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464987365p2/16254355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2320726998?book_show_action=true">Mar 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/16254355-matthew">Matthew</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/32298874-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Sci-Fi Character Based Story Fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=book-a-book-club">book-a-book-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=hoopla">hoopla</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2320726998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4665896995914005706">I had been hearing a lot about this book from some booktubers I follow. Surprisingly, that is the only place I had heard about this – I don’t remember seeing it in my Goodreads feed when others were reading it. But, since a few people said it was their favorite book they read last year, I figured it was worth giving it a try.<br/><br/>Whenever I dig into a Sci-Fi or Fantasy novel, I usually find the new world a bit difficult to get into. That was honestly the case with this book as well; lots of new plane</span>
  <span id="freeText4665896995914005706" style="display:none">I had been hearing a lot about this book from some booktubers I follow. Surprisingly, that is the only place I had heard about this – I don’t remember seeing it in my Goodreads feed when others were reading it. But, since a few people said it was their favorite book they read last year, I figured it was worth giving it a try.<br /><br />Whenever I dig into a Sci-Fi or Fantasy novel, I usually find the new world a bit difficult to get into. That was honestly the case with this book as well; lots of new planets, species, technology, politics, etc. Each of these things took a bit to get used to. But, once I got used to them it was very easy to sit back and enjoy the story. So, going in, be prepared for that.<br /><br />I mentioned the new world being difficult to get into and there being a lot of world building. However, in this case it was more species building than anything. This makes sense because the main focus of this story, in my opinion, is relationships and people with different backgrounds and personalities getting along. It really is a great book if you are into character focused stories.<br /><br />Regarding the story, with the focus being on the characters, I feel like the story kind of took the backseat. This is not a bad thing in this case. It seems to me the author wanted us to experience the people but needed a story to put them in for motivation. I cannot imagine creating a balance with more character and less story while keeping everything moving along is an easy thing to do, but Chambers does a great job. Her focus on smaller anecdotes throughout (planet stops) really helps by adding side stories and giving specific focus on the different characters for a few pages.<br /><br />Sci-Fi fans and fans of powerful character interactions/relationships should check this out. Give yourself a chance to get comfortable with the universe created by Chambers and I think you will be blown away. <br /><br />Side note: With this book and the Lunar Chronicles it seems that "Stars!" is a common Sci-Fi exclamation right now. Anyone else notice that?</span>
  <a data-text-id="4665896995914005706" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473619807" href="/book/show/25786523-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>,

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1282825116975687730"><i>“I can wait for the galaxy outside to get a little kinder.”</i><br/><br/>First thing I have to say is: A+ cover and title choice. It had me in love the moment I first laid my eyes on this book.<br/><br/>To be honest, <i>The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet</i> was not what I expected.<br/>I imagined a romantic and action-packed plot. What I got was an incredibly detailed, imaginably crafted and super lovely space-trip. This novel was more about friendship, trust and acceptance, than anything else. I was everything but disappointe</span>
  <span id="freeText1282825116975687730" style="display:none"><i>“I can wait for the galaxy outside to get a little kinder.”</i><br /><br />First thing I have to say is: A+ cover and title choice. It had me in love the moment I first laid my eyes on this book.<br /><br />To be honest, <i>The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet</i> was not what I expected.<br />I imagined a romantic and action-packed plot. What I got was an incredibly detailed, imaginably crafted and super lovely space-trip. This novel was more about friendship, trust and acceptance, than anything else. I was everything but disappointed, even though my expectations weren't met.<br />The characters are so rich and stunning, their pasts and their history held me in awe.<br /><br />Now this novel is basically one big group hug. I didn't really mind, but it made the plot easily predictable, and towards the end I would have wished for more intruige or excitement, maybe a cliffhanger or something else to spark my interest a little more.<br /><br />This was a laugh-out-loud read, the giggles I spent on this book weren't wasted. Looking forward to the sequel.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_1969278403" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <a title="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)" href="/user/show/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky">Lauren (Shakespeare &amp; Whisky)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32342930-lauren-shakespeare-whisky?shelf=1-and-2-star-books">1-and-2-star-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1969278403" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9246181358890268507">This was so god-damn boring.<br/><br/>I have taken like two weeks to read this. I cringe when I open my e-reader and it automatically loads to this novel. <br/><br/>I can totally understand why people would love this book and <i>if it had even a smidge of actual dramatic tension I would have loved it</i>.<br/><br/>The world building was interesting and detailed. It is not only well- thought out, it is thought-provoking.<br/><br/>So why two stars? <b>There is no dramatic thru- line.</b><br/><br/>What do I mean by this? Questions, mysteries and potential drama</span>
  <span id="freeText9246181358890268507" style="display:none">This was so god-damn boring.<br><br>I have taken like two weeks to read this. I cringe when I open my e-reader and it automatically loads to this novel. <br><br>I can totally understand why people would love this book and <i>if it had even a smidge of actual dramatic tension I would have loved it</i>.<br><br>The world building was interesting and detailed. It is not only well- thought out, it is thought-provoking.<br><br>So why two stars? <b>There is no dramatic thru- line.</b><br><br>What do I mean by this? Questions, mysteries and potential dramas get introduced and are almost immediately resolved. Despite the frequent and frank acknowledgement of sex and relationships the book felt strangely sexless. Despite interesting and round characters, they have nothing interesting to say or do. <br><br>It is like the entire book was written to satisfy the author's love of world building but she forget to include an interesting plot. <br><br>Two perfect examples:<br><br>1.) The ship <i>Wayfinder</i> is attacked by pirates. I was excited! I wanted to know what would happen! But almost immediately the pirates agree to be reasonable, be non-violent, take only as much as they need, and leave enough food and supplies for the ship to get to a resupply station. How interested am I once the drastic tension is sucked from the scene?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1448538320ra/17156685.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm fucking not. <br><br>2.) Soon after another ship asks for help. The adorable mechanic agrees to go fix their ship. It is filled with bombs. OMFG. Excitement! Tension! Three seconds later… "Fixed it."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494421957ra/22713108.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There is then like a <i>huge discussion</i> on why said adorable mechanic has no fear of disabling the rest of the bombs. FFS.<br><br>Anyway, I think I've proven my point. <b>A clever, engaging world where nothing interesting is allowed to happen for longer than a paragraph.</b> <br><br>(BTW I DNF'ed after this scene. Made it past half-way so I deserve the right to rate and review.)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1620934673?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Riley" href="/user/show/23179211-riley">Riley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473619807" href="/book/show/25786523-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=diverse-recs">diverse-recs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=lgbtq-sci-fi">lgbtq-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=sapphic-read">sapphic-read</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1620934673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18292769925454621520">This book was definitely unlike anything I have ever read before. <br/>It is a sci-fi about the crew on a spaceship called <i>The Wayfarer</i>. But don't go into this book expecting an action-packed space adventure. This is a completely character driven book that explores gender, sexuality, race and politics in the most beautiful way.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1797081876" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1797081876" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1797081876?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473619807" href="/book/show/25786523-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">y'ALL</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lesbian-mc">lesbian-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=completed-series">completed-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favourite-covers">favourite-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1797081876" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1111440924062185245"><blockquote>
  <i>There was a nebula there, an explosion of dust and light, the fiery corpse of an ancient giant. Within the gaseous folds slept clusters of unborn stars, shining softly. <br/>She took an inventory of her body. She felt her breath, her blood, the ties binding it all together. Every piece, down to the last atom had been made out here, flung through the open in a moment of violence, until they swirled round and round, churning and coalescing, becoming heavy, weighing each other down. <br/><br/>But not any more,</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1111440924062185245" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>There was a nebula there, an explosion of dust and light, the fiery corpse of an ancient giant. Within the gaseous folds slept clusters of unborn stars, shining softly. <br>She took an inventory of her body. She felt her breath, her blood, the ties binding it all together. Every piece, down to the last atom had been made out here, flung through the open in a moment of violence, until they swirled round and round, churning and coalescing, becoming heavy, weighing each other down. <br><br>But not any more, the pieces were floating free now. They had returned home. She was exactly where she was supposed to be</i>
</blockquote> <br><br><b>THIS BOOK</b> this stunning, beautiful, complex piece of sci-fi. I love you. I love you and you have me so shook. THIS is what my universe looks like, THIS is what I see when I imagine what the universe which if filled with over 60 tillion planets could look like, this is the voice and the direction I yearn to see more science fiction taking<br><br><b>THIS IS SPACE</b> like you've never seen it before<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481189636ra/21395205.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>There's no doubt <i>The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet</i> is absurdly charming. I mean, just that title is bizarre, yet delightful. This whole book is like that. It's <b>ODD</b>, maybe a bit <i>much </i> for some people, but oh my god it's delightful. <br><br>Becky Chambers creates a space story that's unlike any I've read before. The sheer magnitude and complexity of the universe system, and the species that fill it is outstanding on it's own. This is a truly creative and breathtaking novel -- and one which looks at our world today and offers a universe where all we see WORKS, or at least tries to. <i>This is an incredibly progressive book and I love it</i><br><br><blockquote>THIS REVIEW IS MAKING NO SENSE THOUGH<br>I realise I am rambling<br>Oh god there's just so much to say</blockquote><br><br><b>Maybe I should start with what it's about</b>. It's the future. Humans fucked up. Earth is dead, we had to leave. We enter space, live on Mars .... aliens are so fucking real.<br><br>The planet is filled with them .. all different species. There's one's with scales and feathers, some that communicate through swirling colours on their cheeks, some that come in pairs and are non-binary. There's aliens that start as female and become males. There's aliens with power, aliens without power, aliens who's species are going extinct, aliens who are warring with themselves. <br><br>And humans are a blip. Just another species, a new member to the Galactic Commons (Kind of a space European Union) <br><br>But this book isn't about humans -  talking about humans, how very speciescentric of me<br><br>This is about a ship. It's about a group of friends, lovers, enemies. This is about the crew aboard the <i>Wayfarer</i>, a multi-species tunneling ship who's job it is is to create wormholes in space that essentially act as space highways. <br><br>The crew of the Wayfarer: You got your humans, Rosemary, Kizzy, Jenks, Corbin and Ashby. You got an Aandrisk, Sissix, A Grum, Dr Chef. And a Sianiat, Ohan. And their AI, Lovey. <br>This crew is hired to create a new tunnel to the new members of the GC, the Toremi. <br><br>But it's not even about that. It's about all the stuff in the middle, about <i>what happens</i> on the long way to that small, angry planet. And it's <b>amazing</b>, it's incredible. It's complex. It's actually such a joyous read. <br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481189636ra/21395206.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>HONESTLY, this review is sucking. <br>So here's what I'm gonna do<br><br>This book is underrated, and it's amazing. <br>And I think everyone needs to read it, because it's so fucking clever. <br>So here is<br><br><b>
  <u>TEN REASONS YOU (YES YOU) SHOULD READ THE LONG WAY TO A SMALL, ANGRY PLANET</u>
</b><br><br>1: <b>The title is a fucking delight.</b> Like, I know thats maybe not gonna instantly sell you on the book but seriously the title is so good and I love it. It's absurdly catchy.<br><br>2: <b>The cover is pretty</b> (don't even TELL ME you've never judged books by their covers smhhh)<br><br>3:<b> The world building is detailed and complex.</b> Do not think this book is simple, it is not. The universe is expansive, and it's features so many different species of aliens. All with their own cultures, behaviours, politics, and features. These are aliens who's beliefs so fundamentally challenged mine as a human, and not only that <b>THE FACT EVERYONE IS SO DIFFERENT IS SO OFTEN ADDRESSED</b>. This is a system where aliens actively try to understand and comprehend eachother, but often end up doing things that are insensitive on accident. This is a universe where things are not the binary ideas us humans cling to. There are aliens who have no gender and so use they/them pronouns !! there are aliens who are cold-blooded !! there are aliens who cannot speak !! there are aliens who lay eggs !! there are aliens who have multiple family systems and aliens who suffer from specific alien viruses and aliens of all different shape, colour, type, culture. It's amazing, and the intricate way the humans/aliens try to relate to eachother, and be compassionate of eachother despite fundamental differences in their morality/beliefs/culture is amazing. <br><br>4: <b>It's a new take on science fiction. </b> This book felt really new to me in a genre that's been written in ALOT. For a start, its got a distinctly feminine voice. Men dominate science fiction, and having a book that felt feminine, that felt a little more empathetic (?) in some ways then science fiction which is often straightforward and factual was refreshing. I loved that. I also loved the complexity of the aliens (Because I hate that in alot of sci-fi aliens are like humans). Overrall, it just felt new. It's felt refreshing. <br><br>5: <b>It's accessible to non-sci fi readers</b> If you don't read Sci-fi alot, I think you can still really really like this. It also does away with the complex terminology and space mumbo jumbo that often pervades science fiction and instead is just about people - who happen to be in space. And while it's still got many sci-fi elements, it's not cold or withdrawn like some sci-fi. This lets you get involved, lets you immerse yourselves in the characters lives and in their world and feels much more friendly and welcoming then some science fiction on the market. <br><br>6: <b>It is incredibly diverse</b>. The aliens aside, it features LGBT+ and non-binary characters, an lgbt couple, as well as people of varying race/culture and religion. It includes a main character with dwarfism (which does not dominate his character) and all these issues are ..... well they're not issues. That's the amazing thing. These are not stories ABOUT people being gay or having physical disabilities. These are just characters, and some of them happen to be gay ect and it's okay. It's all okay, and it's amazing. I also love, like LOVE the humans didn't speak English. I love that it's moved beyond thinking of our world so narrowly and has so incredibly expanded the horizons. I love that some of the aliens use xe pronouns, or some don't have any gender, some change gender to male or female or neither. I love that even amongst humans there are different pieces of history that have effected human nature and that the diversity is treated so complexly it's honestly mindblowing and you need to read it to understand<br><br>7: <b>It's character driven</b> This may be a turning away point for some people, but if you, like me, love stories which revolve around characters you'll love this. This is very much about the crew on board the ship, and develops them and their relationships thoroughly. It's also just about people in general trying to understand and relate to each other, and if you're a fan of that I PROMISE YOU WILL LOVE THIS. The characters are incredibly well constructed, and I genuinely fell in love with every single one. They are all different, and all multi-layered people but each is so special and I love them all. Every character was incredibly well constructed right down to their fears, beliefs and morality being incorporated into the book and they drove this story amazingly. It also focusses on so many different types of relationships, found families, platonic and romantic relationships, between different species, between humans and AI's. Between all sorts. It's the best. Incredible female characters !! Including female mechanics (don't see often !!) and just kick ass girls in general. Also the male characters are great friends and lovers (some of them) but are not tropey and gross and I just LOVE the characters so much<br><br>8: <b>AI THAT MAKES YOU FEEL</b>. In this world, AI are a big deal and there are full committee's dedicated to AI rights. And the AI in this is so ... so lovely and will tear your heart out <br><br>9: <b>It's progressive, thoughtful, and offers a little bit of a metaphor for our world now</b>. This world, this beautiful universe where people attempt really hard to understand despite obvious differences could be us. It looks at alot of social issues and implements them into the world in a positive way. It also touches up on some ways we can be more tolerant. For example, I loved how Rosemary is always reminding herself to be less "human-centric" (ie. judge other cultures by human standards). I thought it was a good metaphor for trying not to be eurocentric. I love that this world offers legitimiate solutions and ideas as to how we can overcome cultural barriers to make living and working alongside people we may not understand completely easier, and it's a book which preaches so much respect and love of neighbour. It's also a bit philosophical and thoughtful, looks alot into human nature and the human condition, and some of the things we do as people which are kind of crazy. <br><br>10: <b>It's a bit of fun</b> Despite everything, it's an incredibly fun book. A wild ride through unfamiliar space, with a crew thats both wacky and wonderful. The characters are insane, and some of the things they do are just odd. Meeting the new species, experiencing cultures which are crazily bizarre is fun, and getting to picture and imagine all these new species with their outlandish appearances and behaviours was honestly a bit of an imagination workout -- which I LOVE. It's just a feel good book, in a feel good world where everything seems a little less <i>bad</i> and so it was nice to inhibit for a while. <br><br><b>A BOOK FOR FANS OF: Illuminae (for alot of reasons), The Raven Cycle (if you like how it's abt characters you'll like this too), Enders Game, Star Wars, and dozens of others.<br>I really think this is a book alot of people could enjoy. <br><br><blockquote><i>“All you can do, Rosemary – all any of us can do – is work to be something positive instead. That is a choice that every sapient must make every day of their life. The universe is what we make of it. It’s up to you to decide what part you will play.” </i></blockquote>
<br><br><b>ACTUAL RATING: 4.5* !<br><br></b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1111440924062185245" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1808896031" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1808896031" />
    <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna"><img alt="Lady Luna. ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575639837p2/53385361.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1808896031?book_show_action=true">Dec 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25201920-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=okay-shelf">okay-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1808896031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7112293091170837873"><b>3/5 ★★★</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"A black hole was the perfect place to contemplate death. There was nothing in the universe that could last forever. Not stars. Not matter. Nothing.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book had me on the fence for either a three or four star rating, I settled for 3.5 right smack bang in the middle. Haha.<br/>I'm going keep this review short & sweet.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480988492i/21371965._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“It was more the prospect of getting mugged. Or harassed. Or stabbed. She’d seen a few people that definitely looked stabby.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>I picked this book up after </span>
  <span id="freeText7112293091170837873" style="display:none"><b>3/5 ★★★</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"A black hole was the perfect place to contemplate death. There was nothing in the universe that could last forever. Not stars. Not matter. Nothing.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>This book had me on the fence for either a three or four star rating, I settled for 3.5 right smack bang in the middle. Haha.<br>I'm going keep this review short &amp; sweet.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480988492i/21371965._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“It was more the prospect of getting mugged. Or harassed. Or stabbed. She’d seen a few people that definitely looked stabby.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I picked this book up after I saw two of my favourite GR users reading it. The thing with this book is that it's a character focused plot, yes I normally like character focused plots but I just found this book to be boring and very 'meh', the plot was so boring &amp; lacked action. I feel like this book would be better suited as a TV series rather then a book.<br><br>So basically it's about a crew onboard a long haul space craft. They are like miners who punch holes in space. The captain looks after his family so wants better jobs, he sees a job advertised to travel to a planet that is currently at war. A whole bunch of shit happens and that's basically the plot haha. So like I said I was bored, it was like days of our lives only with aliens. I've seen this book compared to Startrek.. This book is much much better then Startrek (sorry guys) Startrek is the biggest load of wank I've ever seen in my life. Startrek rant over.. The pacing of the book was far to slow for me. I will check out the other books in this series but it definitely isn't a favourite.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1480988492i/21371966.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>"and all the people seeing us fly by are like, oh my stars, look at that totally amazing ship, what genius tech patched together such a thing, and I’m like, oh, that’s me, Kizzy Shao, you can all name your babies after me – whooosh"</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>I did however fall head over heels with all the members aboard the wayfarer, all the characters were so special in their own way. My favourite characters were Kizzy, Jenks &amp; Ashby. Whatever planet Kizzy is from I think I was born there aswell, she's the most relatable character I've ever come across, I swear we are twins :). Seriously I wish my love bun was a real person we would be BFFL &lt;3<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>'“Well, if you’re going to live on this ship, you’re going to have to learn to speak Kizzy.”</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>Things I liked;</b><br>◆ I love the diversity, all characters were different. I also liked the fact that it was very realistic, all the aliens judged everyone for being different just like real life. Some aliens were so racist, but then there was Rosemary who is human and intrigued by the other races, she was so curious and respectful of everyone. Definitely not a hater haha.<br>◆ I love the fact that on the wayfarer they are one big happy family, it didn't matter where you came from or what race you were they were all treated equally and everyone was a part of the crew :')<br>◆ I absolutely adored the aspect of forbidden love; man with alien, man with AI &amp; interspecies girl on girl relationships.<br>◆ I LOVED all characters I felt like I was a member of the wayfarer while reading it.<br>◆I LOVED KIZZY, everything about her was amazing.<br>◆ It was hilarious that half the crew were stoners haha.<br>◆ It made me laugh out loud everytime I read it, seriously the crew are so funny !<br>◆ Most importantly the friendship between the characters had me feeling all warm and fuzzy ! It was definitely filled with rainbows, puppy dogs &amp; kittens :D<br><br><b>Things I didn't like;</b><br>◆ Slow paced plot.<br>◆ Lack of action<br>◆ When the people robbed their ship, they let it happen.. Like common buy some fucking guns and kill those bastards.<br>◆ Boring Plot (like seriously where's the action at)<br>◆ Hardly any blood, guts and killing (like I was dying of blood thirst while reading this)<br><br>The pros out way the cons and this was a great, lighthearted read that I really enjoyed reading it was so fun ! :).<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <i>“Punch ‘em in the face! Monkeys like it, too!”<br>“Hey. Kizzy,” Jenks said.<br>“I ate a har - monica! These socks — match — my hat!”<br>“Kizzy.”<br>“A tool clattered to the ground. Kizzy’s hands clenched into fists as the music swelled to a stormy crescendo. She danced atop the shuddering ladder, her head still in the ceiling. “Socks! Match — my hat! Socks! Match — my hat! Step on — some — sweet — toast! Socks! Match — my hat!”<br>“Kizzy!”<br><br>“Huh. Well, if this band hates the establishment that much, then I doubt they’ll care about me making up my own words. They can’t oppress me with their ‘correct lyrics.’ Fuck the system.”</i>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br>Who I would recommend this to? to all fans of sci fi or anyone looking for something different &amp; diverse with a character driven plot. Also if your anything like me and obsessed with space &amp; the unknown you will enjoy reading this.</span>

<div id="review_1635845744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1635845744" />
    <a title="Nick Imrie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5906293-nick-imrie"><img alt="Nick Imrie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591436280p2/5906293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1635845744?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nick Imrie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nick Imrie" href="/user/show/5906293-nick-imrie">Nick Imrie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25201920-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5906293-nick-imrie?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5906293-nick-imrie?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1635845744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4168080578302335087">I find myself in a difficult position reviewing this book. It's an astonishingly bad book, but it was recommended highly by many people whose opinions I respect. It's hard for me to know if I'm judging this book fairly on its own merits or comparing it unfavourably with the book I was expecting. I was expecting senstive, nuanced writing, good enough to be classed as literary fiction; optimistic and joyful SF in the style of <i>Star Trek</i> or <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian' title='The Martian by Andy Weir' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Martian</a>; and maybe a little bit of adventure or mystery</span>
  <span id="freeText4168080578302335087" style="display:none">I find myself in a difficult position reviewing this book. It's an astonishingly bad book, but it was recommended highly by many people whose opinions I respect. It's hard for me to know if I'm judging this book fairly on its own merits or comparing it unfavourably with the book I was expecting. I was expecting senstive, nuanced writing, good enough to be classed as literary fiction; optimistic and joyful SF in the style of <i>Star Trek</i> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18007564.The_Martian" title="The Martian by Andy Weir" rel="nofollow noopener">The Martian</a>; and maybe a little bit of adventure or mystery. Instead, I got a book that was relentlessly "Nice". And so, I feel kinda guilty when I criticise it. Look, it's badly written, badly plotted, badly paced, with terrible dialogue, poorly-sketched characters and very little actual science fiction - and yet, when I say so I feel like I'm kicking a kitten! How dare I be so mean to such a "Nice" book?<br /><br />The crew of the Wayfarer are contracted to build a hyperspace tunnel, and must travel a long distance to do so. Although they are a commercial team engaged in engineering, most of the book has a very cosy domestic feel. The characters refer to themselves as a family often, and business disputes never occur and therefore can't effect their cosy relationships. As they journey, the characters visit family and friends or go shopping. Even scenes that could have been dramatic (space pirates or tyrannical border guards) are curiously flat due to their easy resolution.<br />It reminded me very much of 19th or early-20th century children's books in which each rather tame adventure ends with a character learning an important lesson about Doing One's Duty or The Importance of Hard Work - except here they learn about Not Judging Others or The Importance of Pacifism! In each case, turgid chunks of over-explanation are worsened by the poor quality of the writing. It's littered with annoying verbal tics that should have been removed by an editor. The most striking of these was the overuse of the word 'smirk' instead of the word 'smile', in one instance a character even 'gave a fond smirk'.<br /><br />The moralism of the book is especially infuriating because it's often so shallow. Characters learn about the importance of getting along with each other - but not about truly important things. This is difficult to discuss without giving massive spoilers, so I'll try to focus on the least spoilery cases. One of the crew, Sissix, is Aandrisk: a repitilian species who lay eggs. They do not view their young as full people until they are grown and so are very cavalier about their high infant mortality rate.<br /><blockquote>She would never, ever understand the idea that a child, especially an infant, was of more value than an adult who had already gained all the skills needed to benefit the community. The death of a new hatchling was so common as to be expected. The death of a child about to feather, yes, that was sad. But a real tragedy was the loss of an adult with friends and lovers and family.</blockquote><br />But let us consider this for a moment. The Aandrisk are a space-faring species, so it cannot be predators, parasites or disease destroying their young; they would surely have the technology to deal with these things. What else causes high infant mortality in reptiles? Neglect? Cannibalism?<br />This is getting pretty bleak, isn't it? It's not very nice.<br />So, naturally, the entire issue is completely avoided. When the crew visit Sissix home, she is very loving towards two children, who are obviously sentient beings and not half-formed half-people. The callous Aandrisk attitude to children is never seen, just referenced as one of those wacky alien differences that must be tolerated.<br /><br />One of the characters in the book is a sentient AI. By any measure, the AI is a full person. She both thinks and feels. She has desires that do not necessarily align with the needs of her owners. The love story between the AI and a crew member is one of the few plot lines that had genuine consequences. Yet, legally, AI are not people. They can be deleted on a whim and are denied any rights whatsoever, and laws are in place to prevent them acheiving independence. She's an off-the-shelf model that is common on ships through-out the universe. The implication is that there are billions of AI, just like her, through-out the universe held in total, abject slavery.<br />That's not very nice, is it?<br />So, of course, this story line does not touch upon the horror of this galaxy-wide slavery at all. This plot is all about the love story - and the lesson that the characters learn from it is that perhaps they should be a bit nicer and not take the help for granted.<br /><br />I said at the start of this review that 'Niceness' is no excuse for bad writing. But more than this, niceness is a frequent and cowardly excuse for avoiding difficult confrontations and important questions. Through-out this book the world-building sets up ethical dilemmas - questions concerning the definitions of personhood, the rights of robots, medical consent. And everytime, these difficult questions are overlooked in favour of a trite homily on friendship. Eventually the niceness of the crew of the <i>Wayfarer</i> is not heart-warming. It is not charming. It is a total failure to engage meaningfully with the universe around them. A blind preference for easy comfort over true justice.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4168080578302335087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1811114347" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1811114347" />
    <a title="Philip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30863291-philip"><img alt="Philip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527983001p2/30863291.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1811114347?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Philip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Philip" href="/user/show/30863291-philip">Philip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062444134" href="/book/show/27213244-the-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=author-woman">author-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30863291-philip?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1811114347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12631724387390203896">4.25ish stars. <br/> <br/>Somehow this manages to be both sweet and hardcore at the same time. Its characters are people I want to knock a few back with and I don't even drink. Chambers has made them each awesome in their own ways without trying too hard. They're not cool in the way that literary heroes (superheroes, public heroes, unsung heroes, etc.) typically are. They're just legitimately good people who do what they do and watch out for their own. It's refreshing.<br/><br/>It doesn't even bother me a bit that </span>
  <span id="freeText12631724387390203896" style="display:none">4.25ish stars. <br /> <br />Somehow this manages to be both sweet and hardcore at the same time. Its characters are people I want to knock a few back with and I don't even drink. Chambers has made them each awesome in their own ways without trying too hard. They're not cool in the way that literary heroes (superheroes, public heroes, unsung heroes, etc.) typically are. They're just legitimately good people who do what they do and watch out for their own. It's refreshing.<br /><br />It doesn't even bother me a bit that there isn't a ton of plot. Sure there's conflict and some blood-pumping moments but the stories are mostly slice-of-life... in space. Maybe closer to space chorale than space opera. <br /><br />There's a diverse crew aboard the Wayfarer with several species represented. Each of the species that Chambers has conceived are all thoroughly detailed and imagined. One of my favorite things is realizing that, in this universe, humans are just as weird and confusing to these other alien races as the aliens are to us. And I love that the humans weren't elevated to being morally or intelligently superior, or even the most populous or influential species. I feel like that happens too often, authors create alien races that are cool but that lack the <i>humanity</i> that would qualify them as being genuinely good or sympathetic. <br /><br />I was afraid a few times, specifically when Sissix was explaining her culture and the familial structures of her species, that Chambers would sell out and Sissix would have a humanizing "epiphany" realizing that yes! of course it's "right" for me to feel a maternal bond to my hatchlings the way humans do with their children! But that didn't happen. She explained the differences and that's all they were. It wasn't "good" or "bad." They're just differences and it's okay.<br /><br />Now if only we humans could accept that amongst ourselves... :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12631724387390203896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6947520120404362859">2.5 stars. Unpopular opinion time! The first of my two DNFs in the last few weeks. This breezy adventure about a motley crew in an old spaceship was just okay for me. It never captured my imagination, and I ended up putting it down about halfway through and just never picking it back up again. <br/><br/>If diversity and acceptance are deeply important to you, this might be a great read for you. Everybody on the crew of the <i>Wayfarer</i> is diverse (mostly in a space alien but also in a sexuality kind of way) b</span>
  <span id="freeText6947520120404362859" style="display:none">2.5 stars. Unpopular opinion time! The first of my two DNFs in the last few weeks. This breezy adventure about a motley crew in an old spaceship was just okay for me. It never captured my imagination, and I ended up putting it down about halfway through and just never picking it back up again. <br /><br />If diversity and acceptance are deeply important to you, this might be a great read for you. Everybody on the crew of the <i>Wayfarer</i> is diverse (mostly in a space alien but also in a sexuality kind of way) but accepting and loving (well, mostly), conflicts are resolved, love is found, and so on. But other than that diversity-positive element, the plot didn't strike me as anything new or unusual in SF, and diversity and social justice by themselves aren't enough to keep me engaged in an otherwise bland book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6947520120404362859" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_40881903'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40881903-unparalleled"><img alt="Unparalleled" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1532093846l/40881903._SY160_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yqTz8maVOB40ft7o+kR+jzlbPBoTVx8L5ME8UBMqH+iaz2vvZjHmqbpBXjSqihEt901REebigivGODxN7ooNBw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('18ejqyd45igrjgVAsOxBWmKGAGjSCHA9EzMO5iCrczWHrDu2J9w4n6WxhZzgIi74rJBtYye97R0xyg773Qth2g==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15145840464860611369">Becky Chambers is a science fiction author based in Northern California. She is best known for her Hugo Award-winning Wayfarers series, which currently includes The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet, A Closed and Common Orbit, and Record of a Spaceborn Few. Her books have also been nominated for the Arthur C. Clarke Award, the Locus Award, and the Women's Prize for Fiction, among others. Her most </span>
  <span id="freeText15145840464860611369" style="display:none">Becky Chambers is a science fiction author based in Northern California. She is best known for her Hugo Award-winning Wayfarers series, which currently includes The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet, A Closed and Common Orbit, and Record of a Spaceborn Few. Her books have also been nominated for the Arthur C. Clarke Award, the Locus Award, and the Women's Prize for Fiction, among others. Her most recent work is To Be Taught, If Fortunate, a standalone novella.<br /><br />Becky has a background in performing arts, and grew up in a family heavily involved in space science. She spends her free time playing video and tabletop games, keeping bees, and looking through her telescope. Having hopped around the world a bit, she’s now back in her home state, where she lives with her wife. She hopes to see Earth from orbit one day.</span>

The only thing it has going for it is a chance proximity to more popular worlds, making it a decent stopover for ships traveling between the wormholes that keep the Galactic Commons connected. If deep space is a highway, Gora is just your average truck stop.\n\nAt the Five-Hop One-Stop, long-haul spacers can stretch their legs (if they have legs, that is), and get fuel, transit permits, and assorted supplies. The Five-Hop is run by an enterprising alien and her sometimes helpful child, who work hard to provide a little piece of home to everyone passing through.\n\nWhen a freak technological failure halts all traffic to and from Gora, three strangers—all different species with different aims—are thrown together at the Five-Hop. Grounded, with nothing to do but wait, the trio—an exiled artist with an appointment to keep, a cargo runner at a personal crossroads, and a mysterious individual doing her best to help those on the
